## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Task: Write Tests for CockroachDB KV Transaction Conflict Resolution

## Objective
Write unit tests for the transaction conflict resolution logic in CockroachDB's KV layer, covering write-write conflicts, read-write conflicts, and deadlock detection.

## Steps
1. Study the transaction conflict handling in `pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/`
2. Understand the `LockTable` and `ConcurrencyManager` interfaces
3. Study the `TxnWaitQueue` or equivalent conflict resolution mechanism
4. Create a test file in `pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/` with tests for:
   - Write-write conflict detection between two transactions
   - Read-write conflict with different isolation levels
   - Deadlock detection with two transactions waiting on each other
   - Transaction priority-based conflict resolution
   - Lock acquisition timeout behavior
   - Intent resolution after transaction commit/abort

## Key Reference Files
- `pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/concurrency_manager.go`
- `pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/lock_table.go`
- `pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/` — existing tests as pattern

## Success Criteria
- Test file exists in the concurrency package
- Tests cover write-write conflicts
- Tests cover deadlock scenarios
- Tests reference ConcurrencyManager or LockTable

This request should sit tight\\n55: \\t// and wait for a new notification without pushing anyone.\\n56: \\t//\\n57: \\t// It must be the case that there are no lock holders for the associated key\\n58: \\t// if a request is actively waiting in the waitSelf state. That's because if\\n59: \\t// the key is locked by another transaction, the request must be in the\\n60: \\t// waitFor state. A request does not need to actively wait if the only lock\\n61: \\t// that's held on the key belongs to its own transaction, thus making the\\n62: \\t// waitSelf state impossible for held locks.\\n63: \\t//\\n64: \\t// NB: The main motivation of the waitSelf state is to avoid certain\\n65: \\t// dependency cycles by potentially re-ordering the lock's wait queue.\\n66: \\t// Typically, the waitSelf state arises when there are >= 1 locking requests\\n67: \\t// from other transactions between two requests from the same transaction\\n68: \\t// waiting in a lock's wait queue. The conflicting\n110: \t// transaction may be a lock holder of a conflicting lock or a\n111: \t// conflicting request being sequenced through the same lockTable.\n112: \ttxn                   *enginepb.TxnMeta // always non-nil\n113: \tkey                   roachpb.Key       // the key of the conflict\n114: \theld                  bool              // is the conflict a held lock?\n115: \tqueuedLockingRequests int               // how many locking requests are waiting?\n116: \tqueuedReaders         int               // how many readers are waiting?\n117: \n118: \t// Represents the lock strength of the action that the request was trying to\n119: \t// perform when it hit the conflict. E.g. was it trying to perform a (possibly\n120: \t// locking) read or write an Intent?\n121: \tguardStrength lock.Strength\n122: }\n123: \n124: // String implements the fmt.Stringer interface.\n125: func (s waitingState) String() string {\n126: \treturn redact.StringWithoutMarkers(s)\n127: }\n128: \n129: // SafeFormat implements the redact.SafeFormatter interface.\n130: func (s waitingState) SafeFormat(w redact.SafePrinter, _ rune) {\n131: \tswitch s.kind {\n132: \tcase waitFor:\n133: \t\ttarget := redact.SafeString(\"holding lock\")\n134: \t\tif !s.held {\n135: \t\t\ttarget = \"running request\"\n136: \t\t}\n137: \t\tw.Printf(\"wait for txn %s %s @ key %s (queuedLockingRequests: %d, queuedReaders: %d)\",\n138: \t\t\ts.txn.Short(), target, s.key, s.queuedLockingRequests, s.queuedReaders)\n139: \tcase waitSelf:\n140: \t\tw.Printf(\"wait self @ key %s\", s.key)\n141: \tcase waitElsewhere:\n142: \t\tif !s.held {\n143: \t\t\tw.SafeString(\"wait elsewhere by proceeding to evaluation\")\n144: \t\t}\n145: \t\tw.Printf(\"wait elsewhere for txn %s @ key %s\", s.txn.Short(), s.key)\n146: \tcase waitQueueMaxLengthExceeded:\n147: \t\tw.Printf(\"wait-queue maximum length exceeded @ key %s with length %d\",\n148: \t\t\ts.key, s.queuedLockingRequests)\n149: \tcase doneWaiting:\n150: \t\tw.SafeString(\"done waiting\")\n151: \tdefault:\n152: \t\tpanic(\"unhandled waitingState.kind\")\n153: \t}\n154: }\n155: \n156: // Implementation\n157: // TODO(sbhola):\n158: // - metrics about lockTable state to export to observability debug pages:\n159: //   number of locks, number of waiting requests, wait time?, ...\n160: \n161: // The btree for keys that have locks on them.\n162: type treeMu struct {\n163: \tmu syncutil.RWMutex // Protects everything in this struct.\n164: \n165: \t// For assigning sequence numbers to the keyLocks objects as required by\n166: \t// the util/interval/generic type contract.\n167: \tlockIDSeqNum uint64\n168: \n169: \t// Container for all keyLocks structs, inside which per-key lock tracking\n170: \t// is done. This includes information about the lock holder(s), requests being\n171: \t// sequenced through the lock table, and any queues that form on the key\n172: \t// because of read-write or write-write conflicts. Empty[1] keyLocks structs\n173: \t// are garbage collected. Additionally, keys which only have replicated locks\n174: \t// on them and no contending requests may also be garbage collected, as their\n175: \t// state can be recovered from persistent storage.\n176: \t//\n177: \t// [1] Keys that are not locked and have an empty wait-queue.\n178: \tbtree\n179: \n180: \t// numKeysLocked tracks the number of keyLocks structs in the b-tree. It is\n181: \t// primarily used for constraining memory consumption. Ideally, we should be\n182: \t// doing better memory accounting than this.\n183: \tnumKeysLocked atomic.Int64\n184: \n185: \t// For dampening the frequency with which we enforce\n186: \t// lockTableImpl.maxKeysLocked.\n187: \tlockAddMaxLocksCheckInterval uint64\n188: }\n189: \n190: // lockTableImpl is an implementation of lockTable.\n191: //\n192: // Concurrency: in addition to holding latches, we require for a particular\n193: // request ScanAndEnqueue() and CurState() must be called by the same\n194: // thread.\n195: //\n196: // Mutex ordering:   lockTableImpl.enabledMu\n197: //\n198: //\t> treeMu.mu\n199: //\t> keyLocks.mu\n200: //\t> lockTableGuardImpl.mu\n201: ",

The request and guard are\n132:  discarded after this.\n133: \n134: guard-state r=<name>\n135: ----\n136: new|old: state=<state> [txn=<name> ts=<ts>]\n137: \n138:   Calls lockTableGuard.NewStateChan in a non-blocking manner, followed by\n139:   CurState.\n140: \n141: should-wait r=<name>\n142: ----\n143: <bool>\n144: \n145:  Calls lockTableGuard.ShouldWait.\n146: \n147: resolve-before-scanning r=<name>\n148: ----\n149: <intents to resolve>\n150: \n151: enable [lease-seq=<seq>]\n152: ----\n153: \n154:  Calls lockTable.Enable.\n155: \n156: clear [disable]\n157: ----\n158: <state of lock table>\n159: \n160:  Calls lockTable.Clear. Optionally disables the lockTable.\n161: \n162: print\n163: ----\n164: <state of lock table>\n165: \n166: query span=<start>[,<end> | /Max] [max-locks=<int>] [max-bytes=<int>] [uncontended]\n167: ----\n168: \n169:  Queries the lockTable over a given span (or over the entire LT if no span\n170:  provided), returning lock state info up to a maximum number of locks or bytes\n171:  if provided. (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"testing\"\n\t\"time\"\n\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvpb\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/isolation\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/lock\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/lockspanset\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/spanset\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/txnwait\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/roachpb\"\n\tclustersettings TestWriteWriteConflictDetection verifies that the lock table correctly detects\n// write-write conflicts between two transactions.\nfunc TestWriteWriteConflictDetection(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\t// Create a lock table with capacity for this test\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\t// Create two transactions with different UUIDs\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// Create requests for the same key with intent locks\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// First request: txn1 writes to key1\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\t// Second request: txn2 writes to the same key1\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\t// Scan and enqueue first request\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, guard1)\n\trequire.False(t, guard1.ShouldWait(), \"first request should not wait\")\n\n\t// Acquire lock for first request\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Scan and enqueue second request - should find conflict\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, guard2)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait(), \"second request should wait for first transaction's lock\")\n\n\t// Check the waiting state\n\tstate, err := guard2.CurState()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, waitFor, state.kind)\n\trequire.Equal(t, txn1.ID, state.txn.ID)\n\trequire.True(t, state.held)\n\n\t// Release the locks\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n}\n\n// TestReadWriteConflictWithSerializableIsolation verifies that serializable\n// transactions detect read-write conflicts.\nfunc TestReadWriteConflictWithSerializableIsolation(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction writes to key\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: TestTransactionPriorityConflictResolution(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := state.txn.ID)\n\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n}\n\n// TestLockAcquisitionTimout verifies that lock acquisition can timeout.\nfunc TestLockAcquisitionTimeout(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction tries to acquire with a timeout\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:            txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait())\n\n\t// In a real scenario with a deadline, the wait would lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, guard2)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tif guard2_rescan != nil && guard2_rescan.ShouldWait() {\n\t\t// Still waiting on something else or lock not fully resolved\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2_rescan)\n\t} else {\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n\t}\n}\n\n// TestIntentResolutionAfterAbort verifies that locks are released after\n// transaction abort.\nfunc TestIntentResolutionAfterAbort(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\ttxn1 := != nil {\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2_rescan)\n\t} else {\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n\t}\n}\n\n// TestMultipleWritersQueueing verifies that multiple writers form a queue\n// waiting for a lock.\nfunc TestMultipleWritersQueueing(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// Create three transactions\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn3 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1002},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1002},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction acquires lock\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction waits\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait())\n\n\t// Third transaction also waits\n\treq3 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn3,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn3.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq3.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard3, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req3, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard3.ShouldWait())\n\n\t// Verify queue depth\n\tstate3, err := guard3.CurState()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, waitFor, state3.kind)\n\t// The queue should have other waiters\n\trequire.Greater(t, state3.queuedLockingRequests, 0)\n\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard3)\n}\n\n// TestLockStrengthHierarchy verifies that different lock strengths\n// interact correctly.\nfunc txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := TestWriteWriteConflictDetection verifies that the lock table correctly detects\n// write-write conflicts between two transactions.\nfunc TestWriteWriteConflictDetection(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\t// Create a lock table with capacity for this test\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\t// Create two transactions with different UUIDs\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// Create requests for the same key with intent locks\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// First request: txn1 writes to key1\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\t// Scan and enqueue first Once a request\\n32: // has been sequenced, it is free to evaluate without concerns of conflicting\\n33: // with other in-flight requests due to the isolation provided by the manager.\\n34: // This isolation is guaranteed for the lifetime of the request but terminates\\n35: // once the request completes.\\n36: //\\n37: // Transactions require isolation both within requests and across requests. The\\n38: // manager accommodates this by allowing transactional requests to acquire\\n39: // locks, which outlive the requests themselves. Locks extend the duration of\\n40: // the isolation provided over specific keys to the lifetime of the lock-holder\\n41: // transaction itself. They are (typically) only released when the transaction\\n42: // commits or aborts. Other requests that find these locks while being sequenced\\n43: // wait on them to be released in a queue before proceeding. Because locks are\\n44: // checked during sequencing, requests are guaranteed access to all declared\\n45: // keys after they have been sequenced. In other words, locks don't need to be\\n46: // checked again during evaluation.\\n47: //\\n48: // However, at the time of writing, not all locks are stored directly under the\\n49: // manager's control, so not all locks are discoverable during sequencing.\\n50: // Specifically, write intents (replicated, exclusive locks) are stored inline\\n51: // in the MVCC keyspace, so they are not detectable until request evaluation\\n52: // time. To accommodate this form of lock storage, the manager exposes a\\n53: // HandleLockConflictError method, which can be used in conjunction with a retry\\n54: // loop around evaluation to integrate external locks with the concurrency\\n55: // manager structure. In the future, we intend to pull all locks, including\\n56: // those associated with write intents, into the concurrency manager directly\\n57: // through a replicated lock table structure.\\n58: //\\n59: // Fairness is ensured between requests. In general, if any two requests\\n60: // conflict then the request that arrived first will be sequenced first. As\\n61: // such, sequencing guarantees FIFO semantics. The primary exception to this is\\n62: // that a request that is part of a transaction which has already acquired a\\n63: // lock does not need to wait on that lock during sequencing, and can therefore\\n64: // ignore any queue that has formed on the lock. For other exceptions, see the\\n65: // later comment for lockTable.\\n66: //\\n67: // # Internal Components\\n68: //\\n69: // The concurrency manager is composed of a number of internal synchronization,\\n70: // bookkeeping, and queueing structures. Each of these is discussed in more\\n71: // detail on their interface definition. The following diagram details how the\\n72: // components are tied together:\\n73: //\\n74: //\\t+---------------------+---------------------------------------------+\\n75: //\\t| concurrency.Manager |                                             |\\n76: //\\t+---------------------+                                             |\\n77: //\\t|                                                                   |\\n78: //\\t+------------+  acquire  +--------------+        acquire            |\\n79: //\\t  Sequence() |--->--->---| latchManager |<---<---<---<---<---<---+  |\\n80: //\\t+------------+           +--------------+                        |  |\\n81: //\\t|                         / check locks + wait queues            |  |\\n82: //\\t|                        v  if conflict, enter q & drop latches  ^  |\\n83: //\\t|         +---------------------------------------------------+  |  |\\n84: //\\t|         | [ lockTable ]                                     |  |  |\\n85: //\\t|         | [    key1   ]    -------------+-----------------+ |  ^  |\\n86: //\\t|         | [    key2   ]  /  keyLocks:   | lockWaitQueue:  |----<---<---<----+\\n87: //\\t|         | [    key3   ]-{   - lock type | +-[a]<-[b]<-[c] | |  |  |         |\\n88: //\\t|         | [    key4   ]  \\\\  - txn  meta | |  (no latches) |-->-^  |         |\\n89: //\\t|         | [    key5   ]    -------------+-|---------------+ |     |         |\\n90: //\\t|         | [    ...    ]                   v                 |     |         ^\\n91: //\\t|         +---------------------------------|-----------------+     |         | if lock found, HandleLockConflictError()\\n92: //\\t|                 |                         |                       |         |  - enter txnWaitQueue\\n104: //\\t|                 |                                                 |   ^  - drop latches\\n105: //\\t|                 |                                                 |   |  - wait for txn record update\\n106: //\\t|                 |                                                 |   |     |\\n107: //\\t|                 |                                                 |   |     |\\n108: //\\t|                 +--> retain latches --> remain at head of queues ---> evaluate ---> Finish()\\n109: //\\t|                                                                   |\\n110: //\\t+----------+                                                        |\\n111: //\\t  Finish() | ---> exit wait queues ---> drop latches -----------------> respond ...\\n112: //\\t+----------+                                                        |\\n113: //\\t|                                                                   |\\n114: //\\t+-------------------------------------------------------------------+\\n115: //\\n116: // See the comments on individual components for a more detailed look at their\\n117: // interface and inner-workings.\\n118: //\\n119: // At a high-level, a request enters the concurrency manager and immediately\\n120: // acquires latches from the latchManager to serialize access to the keys that\\n121: // it intends to touch. This latching takes into account the keys being\\n122: // accessed, the MVCC timestamp of accesses, and the access method being used\\n123: // (read vs. write) to allow for concurrency where possible. This has the effect\\n124: // of queuing on conflicting in-flight operations until their completion.\\n125: //\\n126: // Once latched, the request consults the lockTable to check for any conflicting\\n127: // locks owned by other transactions. If any are found, the request enters the\\n128: // corresponding lockWaitQueue and its latches are dropped. Requests in the\\n129: // queue wait for the corresponding lock to be released by intent resolution.\\n130: // While waiting, the head of the lockWaitQueue pushes the owner of the lock\\n131: // through a remote RPC that ends up in the pushee's txnWaitQueue. This queue\\n132: // exists on the leaseholder replica of the range that contains the pushee's\\n133: // transaction record. Other entries in the queue wait for the head of the\\n134: // queue, eventually pushing it to detect coordinator failures and transaction\\n135: // deadlocks. Once the lock is released, the head of the queue reacquires\\n136: // latches and attempts to proceed while remaining at the head of that\\n137: // lockWaitQueue to ensure fairness.\\n138: //\\n139: // Once a request is latched and observes no conflicting locks in the lockTable\\n140: // and no conflicting lockWaitQueues that it is not already the head of, the\\n141: // request can proceed to evaluate. During evaluation, the request may insert or\\n142: // remove locks from the lockTable for its own transaction.\\n143: //\\n144: // When the request completes, it exits any lockWaitQueues that it was a part of\\n145: // and releases its latches. However, if the request was successful, any locks\\n146: // that it inserted into the lockTable remain.\\n147: type Manager interface {\\n148: \\tRequestSequencer\\n149: \\tContentionHandler\\n150: \\tLockManager\\n151: \\tTransactionManager\\n152: \\tRangeStateListener\\n153: \\tMetricExporter\\n154: \\tTestingAccessor\\n155: }\\n156: \\n157: // RequestSequencer is concerned with the sequencing of concurrent requests. It\\n158: // is one of the roles of Manager.\\n159: type RequestSequencer interface {\\n160: \\t// SequenceReq acquires latches, checks for locks, and queues behind and/or\\n161: \\t// pushes other transactions to resolve any conflicts. Once sequenced, the\\n162: \\t// request is guaranteed sufficient isolation for the duration of its\\n163: \\t// evaluation, until the returned request guard is released. NOTE: this last\\n164: \\t// part will not be true until replicated locks are pulled into the\\n165: \\t// concurrency manager. This is the normal behavior for a request marked as\\n166: \\t// PessimisticEval. For OptimisticEval, it can optimize by not acquiring\\n167: \\t// locks, and the request must call Guard.CheckOptimisticNoConflicts after\\n168: \\t// evaluation. OptimisticEval is only permitted in the first call to\\n169: \\t// SequenceReq for a Request. A failed OptimisticEval must use\\n170: \\t// PessimisticAfterFailedOptimisticEval, for the immediately following\\n171: \\t// SequenceReq call, if the latches are already held.\\n172: \\t// TODO(sumeer): change OptimisticEval to only queue the latches and not\\n173: \\t// wait for them, so PessimisticAfterFailedOptimisticEval will wait for\\n174: \\t// them.\\n175: \\t//\\n176: \\t// An optional existing request guard can be provided to SequenceReq. This\\n177: \\t// allows the request's position in lock wait-queues to be retained across\\n178: \\t// sequencing attempts. Requests waiting on\\n193: \\t// this Guard will be notified. Latch acquisitions under poison.Policy_Error\\n194: \\t// react to this by failing with a poison.PoisonedError, while requests under\\n195: \\t// poison.Policy_Wait continue waiting, but propagate the poisoning upwards.\\n196: \\t//\\n197: \\t// See poison.Policy for details.\\n198: \\tPoisonReq(*Guard)\\n199: \\n200: \\t// FinishReq marks the request as complete, releasing any protection\\n201: \\t// the request had against conflicting requests and allowing conflicting\\n202: \\t// requests that are blocked on this one to proceed. The guard should not\\n203: \\t// be used after being released.\\n204: \\tFinishReq(context.Context, *Guard)\\n205: }\\n206: \\n207: // ContentionHandler is concerned with handling contention-related errors. This\\n208: // typically involves preparing the request to be queued upon a retry. It is one\\n209: // of the roles of Manager.\\n210: type ContentionHandler interface {\\n211: \\t// HandleLockConflictError consumes a LockConflictError by informing the\\n212: \\t// concurrency manager about the replicated write intent that was missing\\n213: \\t// from its lock table which was found during request evaluation (while\\n214: \\t// holding latches) under the provided lease sequence. After doing so, it\\n215: \\t// enqueues the request that hit the error in the lock's wait-queue (but\\n216: \\t// does not wait) and releases the guard's latches. It returns an updated\\n217: \\t// guard reflecting this change. After the method returns, the original\\n218: \\t// guard should no longer be used. The method is used to perform\\n277: \\t// deadlock detection. See txnWaitQueue for more.\\n278: \\tGetDependents(uuid.UUID) []uuid.UUID\\n279: }\\n280: \\n281: // RangeStateListener is concerned with observing updates to the concurrency\\n282: // manager's range. It is one of the roles of Manager.\\n283: type RangeStateListener interface {\\n284: \\t// OnRangeDescUpdated informs the manager that its range's descriptor has been\\n285: \\t// updated.\\n286: \\tOnRangeDescUpdated(*roachpb.RangeDescriptor)\\n287: \\n288: \\t// OnRangeLeaseUpdated informs the concurrency manager that its range's\\n289: \\t// lease has been updated. The argument indicates whether this manager's\\n290: \\t// replica is the leaseholder going forward.\\n291: \\tOnRangeLeaseUpdated(_ roachpb.LeaseSequence, isLeaseholder bool)\\n292: \\n293: \\t// OnRangeSplit informs the concurrency manager that its range has split off\\n294: \\t// a new range to its RHS.\\n295: \\tOnRangeSplit()\\n296: \\n297: \\t// OnRangeMerge informs the concurrency manager that its range has merged\\n298: \\t// into its LHS neighbor. It is one of the roles of Manager.\\n309: type MetricExporter interface {\\n310: \\t// LatchMetrics returns information about the state of the latchManager.\\n311: \\tLatchMetrics() LatchMetrics\\n312: \\n313: \\t// LockTableMetrics returns information about the state of the lockTable.\\n314: \\tLockTableMetrics() LockTableMetrics\\n315: \\n316: \\t// TODO(nvanbenschoten): provide better observability into the state of the\\n317: \\t// txn wait queue. It is one of the roles of Manager.\\n325: type TestingAccessor interface {\\n326: \\t// TestingLockTableString returns a debug string representing the state of the\\n327: \\t// lockTable.\\n328: \\tTestingLockTableString() string\\n329: \\n330: \\t// TestingTxnWaitQueue returns the concurrency manager's txnWaitQueue.\\n331: \\tTestingTxnWaitQueue() *txnwait.Queue\\n332: \\n333: \\t// TestingSetMaxLocks updates the locktable's lock limit. Optimistic evaluation is used for requests involving\\n344: // limited scans, where the checking of locks and latches may be (partially)\\n345: // postponed until after evaluation, once the limit has been applied and the\\n346: // key spans have been constrained, using Guard.CheckOptimisticNoConflicts.\\n347: // Note that intents (replicated single-key locks) will still be observed\\n348: // during evaluation.\\n349: //\\n350: // The setting can change across different calls to SequenceReq.
