It is one of the roles of Manager.\n325: type TestingAccessor interface {\n326: \t// TestingLockTableString returns a debug string representing the state of the\n327: \t// lockTable.\n328: \tTestingLockTableString() string\n329: \n330: \t// TestingTxnWaitQueue returns the concurrency manager's txnWaitQueue.\n331: \tTestingTxnWaitQueue() *txnwait.Queue\n332: \n333: \t// TestingSetMaxLocks updates the locktable's lock limit. This can be used to\n334: \t// force the locktable to exceed its limit and clear locks.\n335: \tTestingSetMaxLocks(n int64)\n336: }\n337: \n338: ///////////////////////////////////\n339: // External API Type Definitions //\n340: ///////////////////////////////////\n341: \n342: // RequestEvalKind informs the manager of the evaluation kind for the current\n343: // evaluation attempt. Optimistic evaluation is used for requests involving\n344: // limited scans, where the checking of locks and latches may be (partially)\n345: // postponed until after evaluation, once the limit has been applied and the\n346: // key spans have been constrained, using Guard.CheckOptimisticNoConflicts.\n347: // Note that intents (replicated single-key locks) will still be observed\n348: // during evaluation.\n349: //\n350: // The setting can change across different calls to SequenceReq. The\n351: // permissible sequences are:\n352: //   - OptimisticEval: when optimistic evaluation succeeds.\n353: //   - OptimisticEval, PessimisticAfterFailedOptimisticEval, PessimisticEval*:\n354: //     when optimistic evaluation failed.\n355: //   - PessimisticEval+: when only pessimistic evaluation was attempted.\n356: type RequestEvalKind int\n357: \n358: const (\n359: \t// PessimisticEval represents pessimistic locking.\n360: \tPessimisticEval RequestEvalKind = iota\n361: \t// OptimisticEval represents optimistic locking.\n362: \tOptimisticEval\n363: \t// PessimisticAfterFailedOptimisticEval represents a request sequencing\n364: \t// attempt immediately following a failed OptimisticEval.\n365: \tPessimisticAfterFailedOptimisticEval\n366: )\n367: \n368: // Request is the input to Manager.SequenceReq. The struct contains all of the\n369: // information necessary to sequence a KV request and determine which locks and\n370: // other in-flight requests it conflicts with.\n371: type Request struct {\n372: \t// The (optional) transaction that sent the request.\n373: \t// Non-transactional requests do not acquire locks.\n374: \tTxn *roachpb.Transaction\n375: \n376: \t// The timestamp that the request should evaluate at.\n377: \t// Should be set to Txn.ReadTimestamp if Txn is non-nil.\n378: \tTimestamp hlc.Timestamp\n379: \n380: \t// The priority of the request. Only set if Txn is nil.\n381: \tNonTxnPriority roachpb.UserPriority\n382: \n383: \t// The consistency level of the request. Only set if Txn is nil.\n384: \tReadConsistency kvpb.ReadConsistencyType\n385: \n386: \t// The wait policy of the request. Signifies how the request should\n387: \t// behave if it encounters conflicting locks held by other active\n388: \t// transactions.\n389: \tWaitPolicy lock.WaitPolicy\n390: \n391: \t// The maximum amount of time that the batch request will wait while\n392: \t// attempting to acquire a lock on a key or while blocking on an\n393: \t// existing lock in order to perform a non-locking read on a key.\n394: \tLockTimeout time.Duration\n395: \n396: \t// The maximum length of a lock wait-queue that the request is willing\n397: \t// to enter and wait in. Used to provide a release valve and ensure some\n398: \t// level of quality-of-service under severe per-key contention. If set\n399: \t// to a non-zero value and an existing lock wait-queue is already equal\n400: \t// to or exceeding this length, the request will be rejected eagerly\n401: \t// with a WriteIntentError instead of entering the queue and waiting.\n402: \tMaxLockWaitQueueLength int\n403: \n404: \t// AdmissionHeader is the header in the request's BatchRequest. It is plumbed\n405: \t// through for intent resolution admission control.\n406: \tAdmissionHeader kvpb.AdmissionHeader\n407: \n408: \t// The poison.Policy to use for this Request.\n409: \tPoisonPolicy poison.Policy\n410: \n411: \t// The individual requests in the batch.\n412: \tRequests []kvpb.RequestUnion\n413: \n414: \t// The maximal set of spans that the request will access. Latches\n415: \t// will be acquired for these spans.\n416: \t//\n417: \t// Note: ownership of the SpanSet is assumed by the Request once it is\n418: \t// passed to SequenceReq. Only supplied to SequenceReq if the method is\n419: \t// not also passed an exiting Guard.\n420: \tLatchSpans *spanset.SpanSet\n421: \n422: \t// The maximal set of spans within which the request expects to have isolation\n423: \t// from conflicting transactions. The level of isolation for a span is\n424: \t// dictated by its corresponding lock Strength. Conflicting locks within these\n425: \t// spans will be queued on and conditionally pushed.\n426: \t//\n427: \t// Note: ownership of the LockSpanSet is assumed by the Request once it is\n428: \t// passed to SequenceReq. Only supplied to SequenceReq if the method is\n429: \t// not also passed an exiting Guard.\n430: \tLockSpans *lockspanset.LockSpanSet\n431: \n432: \t// The SafeFormatter capable of formatting the request. This is used to enrich\n433: \t// logging with request level information when latches conflict.\n434: \tBaFmt redact.SafeFormatter\n435: \n436: \t// DeadlockTimeout is the amount of time that the request will wait on a lock\n437: \t// before pushing the lock holder's transaction for deadlock detection.\n438: \tDeadlockTimeout time.Duration\n439: }\n440: \n441: // Guard is returned from Manager.SequenceReq. The guard is passed back in to\n442: // Manager.FinishReq to release the request's resources when it has completed.\n443: type Guard struct {\n444: \tReq Request\n445: \tlg  latchGuard\n446: \tlm  latchManager\n447: \tltg lockTableGuard\n448: \t// The latest RequestEvalKind passed to SequenceReq.\n449: \tEvalKind RequestEvalKind\n450: }\n451: \n452: // Response is a slice of responses to requests in a batch. This type is used\n453: // when the concurrency manager is able to respond to a request directly during\n454: // sequencing.\n455: type Response = []kvpb.ResponseUnion\n456: \n457: // Error is an alias for a kvpb.Error.\n458: type Error = kvpb.Error\n459: \n460: // QueryLockTableOptions bundles the options for the QueryLockTableState function.\n461: type QueryLockTableOptions struct {\n462: \tMaxLocks           int64\n463: \tTargetBytes        int64\n464: \tIncludeUncontended bool\n465: }\n466: \n467: // QueryLockTableResumeState bundles the return metadata on the pagination of\n468: // results from the QueryLockTableState function.\n469: type QueryLockTableResumeState struct {\n470: \tResumeSpan   *roachpb.Span\n471: \tResumeReason kvpb.ResumeReason\n472: \n473: \t// ResumeNextBytes represents the size (in bytes) of the next\n474: \t// roachpb.LockStateInfo object that would have been returned by\n475: \t// QueryLockTableState if it were not limited by MaxLocks or TargetBytes.\n476: \t// As such, this value is only set if ResumeSpan, ResumeReason have been set.\n477: \tResumeNextBytes int64\n478: \n479: \t// TotalBytes is the byte size of the roachpb.LockStateInfo objects returned\n480: \t// by QueryLockTableState, and is always set. This value is used to calculate\n481: \t// the remaining quota of bytes (from TargetBytes) that can be used in\n482: \t// querying other ranges served by the same request.\n483: \tTotalBytes int64\n484: }\n485: \n486: ///////////////////////////////////\n487: // Internal Structure Interfaces //\n488: ///////////////////////////////////\n489: \n490: // latchManager serializes access to keys and key ranges. The\n491: // {AcquireOptimistic,CheckOptimisticNoConflicts,WaitUntilAcquired} methods\n492: // are only for use in optimistic latching.\n493: //\n494: // See additional documentation in pkg/storage/spanlatch.\n495: type latchManager interface {\n496: \t// Acquires latches, providing mutual exclusion for conflicting requests.\n497: \tAcquire(context.Context, Request) (latchGuard, *Error)\n498: \n499: \t// AcquireOptimistic is like Acquire in that it inserts latches, but it does\n500: \t// not wait for conflicting latches on overlapping spans to be released\n501: \t// before returning. This should be followed by CheckOptimisticNoConflicts\n502: \t// to validate that not waiting did not violate correctness.\n503: \tAcquireOptimistic(req Request) latchGuard\n504: \n505: \t// CheckOptimisticNoConflicts returns true iff the spans in the provided\n506: \t// spanset do not conflict with existing latches.\n507: \tCheckOptimisticNoConflicts(lg latchGuard, spans *spanset.SpanSet) bool\n508: \n509: \t// WaitUntilAcquired is meant to be called when CheckOptimisticNoConflicts\n510: \t// returned false, or some other occurrence (like conflicting locks) is\n511: \t// causing this request to switch to pessimistic latching.\n512: \tWaitUntilAcquired(ctx context.Context, lg latchGuard) (latchGuard, *Error)\n513: \n514: \t// WaitFor waits for conflicting latches on the specified spans without adding\n515: \t// any latches itself. Fast path for operations that only require flushing out\n516: \t// old operations without blocking any new ones.\n517: \tWaitFor(ctx context.Context, spans *spanset.SpanSet, pp poison.Policy, baFmt redact.SafeFormatter) *Error\n518: \n519: \t// Poison a guard's latches, allowing waiters to fail fast.\n520: \tPoison(latchGuard)\n521: \n522: \t// Release a guard's latches, relinquish its protection from conflicting requests.\n523: \tRelease(ctx context.Context, lg latchGuard)\n524: \n525: \t// Metrics returns information about the state of the latchManager.\n526: \tMetrics() LatchMetrics\n527: }\n528: \n529: // latchGuard is a handle to a set of acquired key latches.\n530: type latchGuard interface{}\n531: \n532: // lockTable holds a collection of locks acquired by in-progress transactions.\n533: // Each lock in the table has a possibly-empty lock wait-queue associated with\n534: // it, where conflicting transactions can queue while waiting for the lock to be\n535: // released.\n536: //\n537: //\t+---------------------------------------------------+\n538: //\t| [ lockTable ]                                     |\n539: //\t| [    key1   ]    -------------+-----------------+ |\n540: //\t| [    key2   ]  /  keyLocks:   | lockWaitQueue:  | |\n541: //\t| [    key3   ]-{   - lock type | <-[a]<-[b]<-[c] | |\n542: //\t| [    key4   ]  \\  - txn meta  |                 | |\n543: //\t| [    key5   ]    -------------+-----------------+ |\n544: //\t| [    ...    ]                                     |\n545: //\t+---------------------------------------------------+\n546: //\n547: // The database is read and written using \"requests\". Transactions are composed\n548: // of one or more requests. Isolation is needed across requests. Additionally,\n549: // since transactions represent a group of requests, isolation is needed across\n550: // such groups. Part of this isolation is accomplished by maintaining multiple\n551: // versions and part by allowing requests to acquire locks. Even the isolation\n552: // based on multiple versions requires some form of mutual exclusion to ensure\n553: // that a read and a conflicting lock acquisition do not happen concurrently.\n554: // The lock table provides both locking and sequencing of requests (in concert\n555: // with the use of latches). The lock table sequences both transactional and\n556: // non-transactional requests, but the latter cannot acquire locks.\n557: //\n558: // Locks outlive the requests themselves and thereby extend the duration of the\n559: // isolation provided over specific keys to the lifetime of the lock-holder\n560: // transaction itself. They are (typically) only released when the transaction\n561: // commits or aborts. Other requests that find these locks while being sequenced\n562: // wait on them to be released in a queue before proceeding. Because locks are\n563: // checked during sequencing, requests are guaranteed access to all declared\n564: // keys after they have been sequenced. In other words, locks don't need to be\n565: // checked again during evaluation.\n566: //\n567: // However, at the time of writing, not all locks are stored directly under\n568: // lock table control, so not all locks are discoverable during sequencing.\n569: // Specifically, write intents (replicated, exclusive locks) are stored inline\n570: // in the MVCC keyspace, so they are often not detectable until request\n571: // evaluation time. To accommodate this form of lock storage, the lock table\n572: // exposes an AddDiscoveredLock method. In the future, we intend to pull all\n573: // locks, including those associated with write intents, into the lock table\n574: // directly.\n575: //\n576: // The lock table also provides fairness between requests. If two requests\n577: // conflict then the request that arrived first will typically be sequenced\n578: // first. There are some exceptions:\n579: //\n580: //   - a request that is part of a transaction which has already acquired a lock\n581: //     does not need to wait on that lock during sequencing, and can therefore\n582: //     ignore any queue that has formed on the lock.\n583: //\n584: //   - contending requests that encounter different levels of contention may be\n585: //     sequenced in non-FIFO order. This is to allow for more concurrency. e.g.\n586: //     if request R1 and R2 contend on key K2, but R1 is also waiting at key K1,\n587: //     R2 could slip past R1 and evaluate.\n588: type lockTable interface {\n589: \trequestQueuer\n590: \n591: \t// ScanAndEnqueue scans over the spans that the request will access and\n592: \t// enqueues the request in the lock wait-queue of any conflicting locks\n593: \t// encountered.\n594: \t//\n595: \t// The first call to ScanAndEnqueue for a given request uses a nil\n596: \t// lockTableGuard and the subsequent calls reuse the previously returned\n597: \t// one. The latches needed by the request must be held when calling this\n598: \t// function.\n599: \tScanAndEnqueue(Request, lockTableGuard) (lockTableGuard, *Error)\n600: \n601: \t// ScanOptimistic takes a snapshot of the lock table for later checking for\n602: \t// conflicts, and returns a guard. It is for optimistic evaluation of\n603: \t// requests that will typically scan a small subset of the spans mentioned\n604: \t// in the Request. After Request evaluation, CheckOptimisticNoConflicts\n605: \t// must be called on the guard.\n606: \tScanOptimistic(Request) lockTableGuard\n607: \n608: \t// Dequeue removes the request from its lock wait-queues. It should be\n609: \t// called when the request is finished, whether it evaluated or not. The\n610: \t// guard should not be used after being dequeued.\n611: \t//\n612: \t// This method does not release any locks. This method must be called on the\n613: \t// last guard returned from ScanAndEnqueue for the request, even if one of\n614: \t// the (a) lockTable calls that use a lockTableGuard parameter, or (b) a\n615: \t// lockTableGuard call, returned an error. The method allows but does not\n616: \t// require latches to be held.\n617: \tDequeue(lockTableGuard)\n618: \n619: \t// AddDiscoveredLock informs the lockTable of a lock which is wasn't\n620: \t// previously tracking that was discovered during evaluation under the\n621: \t// provided lease sequence.\n622: \t//\n623: \t// The method is called when an exclusive replicated lock held by a\n624: \t// different transaction is discovered when reading the MVCC keys during\n625: \t// evaluation of this request. It adds the lock and enqueues this requester\n626: \t// in its wait-queue. It is required that request evaluation discover such\n627: \t// locks before acquiring its own locks, since the request needs to repeat\n628: \t// ScanAndEnqueue. When consultTxnStatusCache=true, and the transaction\n629: \t// holding the lock is known to be pushed or finalized, the lock is not added\n630: \t// to the lock table and instead tracked in the list of locks to resolve in\n631: \t// the lockTableGuard.\n632: \t//\n633: \t// The lease sequence is used to detect lease changes between the when\n634: \t// request that found the lock started evaluating and when the discovered\n635: \t// lock is added to the lockTable. If there has been a lease change between\n636: \t// these times, information about the discovered lock may be stale, so it is\n637: \t// ignored.\n638: \t//\n639: \t// A latch consistent with the access desired by the guard must be held on\n640: \t// the span containing the discovered lock's key.\n641: \t//\n642: \t// The method returns a boolean indicating whether the discovered lock was\n643: \t// properly handled either by adding it to the lockTable or storing it in\n644: \t// the list of locks to resolve in the lockTableGuard (both cases return\n645: \t// true) or whether it was ignored because the lockTable is currently\n646: \t// disabled (false).\n647: \tAddDiscoveredLock(\n648: \t\tfoundLock *roachpb.Lock, seq roachpb.LeaseSequence,\n649: \t\tconsultTxnStatusCache bool, guard lockTableGuard,\n650: \t) (bool, error)\n651: \n652: \t// AcquireLock informs the lockTable that a new lock was acquired or an\n653: \t// existing lock was updated.\n654: \t//\n655: \t// The TxnMeta associated with the lock acquisition must be the same one used\n656: \t// when the request scanned the lockTable initially. It must only be called in\n657: \t// the evaluation phase, before calling Dequeue, which means all latches\n658: \t// needed by the request are held. The key must be in the request's lock span\n659: \t// set with the appropriate strength. Currently, the only strength with which a\n660: \t// lock can be acquired is Intent[1]. This contract ensures that the lock is\n661: \t// not held in a conflicting manner by a different transaction.\n662: \t// Acquiring a lock that is already held by a transaction upgrades the lock's\n663: \t// timestamp and strength. Any prior sequence numbers at which the lock was\n664: \t// previously held and has since been rolled back are no longer tracked as\n665: \t// well.\n666: \t//\n667: \t// [1] We are in an intermediate state where KV ignores lock strength supplied\n668: \t// by SQL and acquires all locks with Intent locking strength. Notably, this\n669: \t// includes in-memory Exclusive locks acquired for `SELECT FOR UPDATE` queries\n670: \t// as well. While the Intent strength verbiage might be a bit surprising,\n671: \t// there is no meaningful difference when it comes to conflict resolution\n672: \t// between a lock and a request. This is a temporary state, which is bound to\n673: \t// change as we go about supporting additional locking strengths in the lock\n674: \t// table.\n675: \t//\n676: \t// For replicated locks, this must be called after the corresponding write\n677: \t// intent has been applied to the replicated state machine.\n678: \tAcquireLock(*roachpb.LockAcquisition) error\n679: \n680: \t// UpdateLocks informs the lockTable that an existing lock or range of locks\n681: \t// was either updated or released.\n682: \t//\n683: \t// The method is called during intent resolution. For spans containing\n684: \t// Replicated locks, this must be called after intent resolution has been\n685: \t// applied to the replicated state machine. The method itself, however,\n686: \t// ignores the Durability field in the LockUpdate. It can therefore be\n687: \t// used to update locks for a given transaction for all durability levels.\n688: \t//\n689: \t// A latch with SpanReadWrite must be held on span with the lowest timestamp\n690: \t// at which any of the locks could be held. This is explained below.\n691: \t//\n692: \t// Note that spans can be wider than the actual keys on which locks were\n693: \t// acquired, and it is ok if no locks are found or locks held by other\n694: \t// transactions are found (for those lock this call is a noop).\n695: \t//\n696: \t// For COMMITTED or ABORTED transactions, all locks are released.\n697: \t//\n698: \t// For PENDING or STAGING transactions, the behavior is:\n699: \t//\n700: \t// - All replicated locks known to the lockTable are dropped. This is not\n701: \t//   because those intents are necessarily deleted, but because in the\n702: \t//   current code where intents are not managed by the lockTable (this will\n703: \t//   change when we have a segregated lock table), we do not want to risk\n704: \t//   code divergence between lockTable and mvccResolveWriteIntent: the\n705: \t//   danger is that the latter removes or changes an intent while the\n706: \t//   lockTable retains it, and a waiter is stuck forever.\n707: \t//\n708: \t//   Note that even the conservative behavior of dropping locks requires\n709: \t//   that intent resolution acquire latches using the oldest timestamp at\n710: \t//   which the intent could have been written: if the intent was at ts=5 and\n711: \t//   the intent resolution is using ts=10 (since the transaction has been\n712: \t//   pushed), there is a race where a reader at ts=8 can be concurrently\n713: \t//   holding latches and the following bad sequence occurs (both thread1 and\n714: \t//   thread2 are concurrent since their latches do not conflict):\n715: \t//\n716: \t//   - [thread1-txn1] reader sees intent at ts=5\n717: \t//   - [thread2-txn2] intent resolution changes that intent to ts=10\n718: \t//   - [thread2-txn2] updateLocks is called and lock is removed since it is a\n719: \t//     replicated lock.\n720: \t//   - [thread1-txn1] reader calls addDiscoveredLock() for ts=5.\n721: \t//\n722: \t//   Now the lockTable thinks there is a lock and subsequent pushes of txn2\n723: \t//   by txn1 will do nothing since the txn2 is already at timestamp 10. Txn1\n724: \t//   will unnecessarily block until txn2 is done.\n725: \t//\n726: \t// - Unreplicated locks:\n727: \t//   - for epochs older than txn.Epoch, locks are dropped.\n728: \t//   - locks in the current epoch that are at a TxnMeta.Sequence\n729: \t//     contained in IgnoredSeqNums are dropped.\n730: \t//   - the remaining locks are changed to timestamp equal to\n731: \t//     txn.WriteTimestamp.\n732: \tUpdateLocks(*roachpb.LockUpdate) error\n733: \n734: \t// PushedTransactionUpdated informs the lock table that a transaction has been\n735: \t// pushed and is either finalized or has been moved to a higher timestamp.\n736: \t// This is used by the lock table in a best-effort manner to avoid waiting on\n737: \t// locks of finalized or pushed transactions and telling the caller via\n738: \t// lockTableGuard.ResolveBeforeScanning to resolve a batch of intents.\n739: \tPushedTransactionUpdated(*roachpb.Transaction)\n740: \n741: \t// QueryLockTableState returns detailed metadata on locks managed by the lockTable.\n742: \tQueryLockTableState(span roachpb.Span, opts QueryLockTableOptions) ([]roachpb.LockStateInfo, QueryLockTableResumeState)\n743: \n744: \t// Metrics returns information about the state of the lockTable.\n745: \tMetrics() LockTableMetrics\n746: \n747: \t// String returns a debug string representing the state of the lockTable.\n748: \tString() string\n749: \n750: \t// TestingSetMaxLocks updates the locktable's lock limit. This can be used to\n751: \t// force the locktable to exceed its limit and clear locks.\n752: \tTestingSetMaxLocks(maxLocks int64)\n753: }\n754: \n755: // lockTableGuard is a handle to a request as it waits on conflicting locks in a\n756: // lockTable or as it holds a place in lock wait-queues as it evaluates.\n757: type lockTableGuard interface {\n758: \t// ShouldWait must be called after each ScanAndEnqueue. The request should\n759: \t// proceed to evaluation if it returns false, else it releases latches and\n760: \t// listens to the channel returned by NewStateChan.\n761: \tShouldWait() bool\n762: \n763: \t// NewStateChan returns the channel to listen on for notification that the\n764: \t// state may have changed. If ShouldWait returns true, this channel will\n765: \t// have an initial notification. Note that notifications are collapsed if\n766: \t// not retrieved, since it is not necessary for the waiter to see every\n767: \t// state transition.\n768: \tNewStateChan() chan struct{}\n769: \n770: \t// CurState returns the latest waiting state.\n771: \tCurState() (waitingState, error)\n772: \n773: \t// ResolveBeforeScanning lists the locks to resolve before scanning again.\n774: \t// This must be called after:\n775: \t// - the waiting state has transitioned to doneWaiting.\n776: \t// - if locks were discovered during evaluation, it must be called after all\n777: \t//   the discovered locks have been added.\n778: \tResolveBeforeScanning() []roachpb.LockUpdate\n779: \n780: \t// CheckOptimisticNoConflicts uses the LockSpanSet representing the spans that\n781: \t// were actually read, to check for conflicting locks, after an optimistic\n782: \t// evaluation. It returns true if there were no conflicts. See\n783: \t// lockTable.ScanOptimistic for context. Note that the evaluation has\n784: \t// already seen any intents (replicated single-key locks) that conflicted,\n785: \t// so this checking is practically only going to find unreplicated locks\n786: \t// that conflict.\n787: \tCheckOptimisticNoConflicts(*lockspanset.LockSpanSet) (ok bool)\n788: \n789: \t// IsKeyLockedByConflictingTxn returns whether the specified key is locked by\n790: \t// a conflicting transaction in the lockTableGuard's snapshot of the lock\n791: \t// table, given the caller's own desired locking strength. If so, true is\n792: \t// returned and so is the lock holder. If the lock is held by the transaction\n793: \t// itself, there's no conflict to speak of, so false is returned.\n794: \t//\n795: \t// This method is used by requests in conjunction with the SkipLocked wait\n796: \t// policy to determine which keys they should skip over during evaluation.\n797: \t//\n798: \t// If the supplied lock strength is locking (!= lock.None), then any queued\n799: \t// locking requests that came before the lockTableGuard will also be checked\n800: \t// for conflicts. This helps prevent a stream of locking SKIP LOCKED requests\n801: \t// from starving out regular locking requests. In such cases, true is\n802: \t// returned, but so is nil.\n803: \tIsKeyLockedByConflictingTxn(context.Context, roachpb.Key, lock.Strength) (bool, *enginepb.TxnMeta, error)\n804: }\n805: \n806: // lockTableWaiter is concerned with waiting in lock wait-queues for locks held\n807: // by conflicting transactions. It ensures that waiting requests continue to\n808: // make forward progress even in the presence of faulty transaction coordinators\n809: // and transaction deadlocks.\n810: //\n811: // The waiter implements logic for a request to wait on conflicting locks in the\n812: // lockTable until they are released. Similarly, it implements logic to wait on\n813: // conflicting requests ahead of the caller's request in any lock wait-queues\n814: // that it is a part of.\n815: //\n816: // This waiting state responds to a set of state transitions in the lock table:\n817: //   - a conflicting lock is released\n818: //   - a conflicting lock is updated such that it no longer conflicts\n819: //   - a conflicting request in the lock wait-queue acquires the lock\n820: //   - a conflicting request in the lock wait-queue exits the lock wait-queue\n821: //\n822: // These state transitions are typically reactive - the waiter can simply wait\n823: // for locks to be released or lock wait-queues to be exited by other actors.\n824: // Reacting to state transitions for conflicting locks is powered by the\n825: // LockManager and reacting to state transitions for conflicting lock\n826: // wait-queues is powered by the RequestSequencer interface.\n827: //\n828: // However, in the case of transaction coordinator failures or transaction\n829: // deadlocks, a state transition may never occur without intervention from the\n830: // waiter. To ensure forward-progress, the waiter may need to actively push\n831: // either a lock holder of a conflicting lock or the head of a conflicting lock\n832: // wait-queue. This active pushing requires an RPC to the leaseholder of the\n833: // conflicting transaction's record, and will typically result in the RPC\n834: // queuing in that leaseholder's txnWaitQueue. Because this can be expensive,\n835: // the push is not immediately performed. Instead, it is only performed after a\n836: // delay.\n837: type lockTableWaiter interface {\n838: \t// WaitOn accepts and waits on a lockTableGuard that has returned true from\n839: \t// ShouldWait.\n840: \t//\n841: \t// The method should be called after dropping any latches that a request\n842: \t// has acquired. It returns when the request is at the front of all lock\n843: \t// wait-queues and it is safe to re-acquire latches and scan the lockTable\n844: \t// again.\n845: \tWaitOn(context.Context, Request, lockTableGuard) *Error\n846: \n847: \t// ResolveDeferredIntents resolves the batch of intents if the provided\n848: \t// error is nil. The batch of intents may be resolved more efficiently than\n849: \t// if they were resolved individually.\n850: \tResolveDeferredIntents(context.Context, kvpb.AdmissionHeader, []roachpb.LockUpdate) *Error\n851: }\n852: \n853: // txnWaitQueue holds a collection of wait-queues for transaction records.\n854: // Conflicting transactions, known as \"pushers\", sit in a queue associated with\n855: // an extant transaction that they conflict with, known as the \"pushee\", and\n856: // wait for the pushee transaction to commit or abort.\n857: //\n858: // Typically, waiting for a pushee's transaction record to undergo a state\n859: // transition is sufficient to satisfy a pusher transaction. Reacting to state\n860: // transitions for conflicting transactions is powered by the TransactionManager\n861: // interface.\n862: //\n863: // Just like with the lockTableWaiter, there are cases where reacting to state\n864: // transitions alone in insufficient to make forward progress. However, unlike\n865: // with the lockTableWaiter, the location of the txnWaitQueue on the range\n866: // containing the conflicting transaction's record instead of on the range\n867: // containing the conflicting transaction's lock presents an opportunity to\n868: // actively resolve these situations. This is because a transaction's record\n869: // reflects its authoritative status.\n870: //\n871: // The first of these situations is failure of the conflicting transaction's\n872: // coordinator. This situation comes in two flavors:\n873: //   - before a transaction has been finalized (committed or aborted)\n874: //   - after a transaction has been finalized but before all of its intents have\n875: //     been resolved\n876: //\n877: // In the first of these flavors, the transaction record may still have a\n878: // PENDING status. Without a live transaction coordinator heartbeating it, the\n879: // record will eventually expire and be abortable. The the second of these\n880: // flavors, the transaction's record will already be committed or aborted.\n881: // Regardless of which case the push falls into, once the transaction record\n882: // is observed in a finalized state, the push will succeed, kick off intent\n883: // resolution, and return to the sender.\n884: //\n885: // The second of these situations is transaction deadlock. Deadlocks occur when\n886: // the lock acquisition patterns of two or more transactions interact in such a\n887: // way that a cycle emerges in the \"waits-for\" graph of transactions. To break\n888: // this cycle, one of the transactions must be aborted or it is impossible for\n889: // any of the transactions that are part of the deadlock to continue making\n890: // progress.\n891: //\n892: // The txnWaitQueue provides a mechanism for detecting these cycles across a\n893: // distributed graph of transactions. Distributed deadlock detection works by\n894: // having each pusher transaction that is waiting in the queue for a different\n895: // transaction periodically query its own record using a QueryTxn request. While\n896: // on the pusher's own transaction record range, the QueryTxn request uses the\n897: // GetDependents method to collect the IDs of all locally-known transactions\n898: // that are waiting for the pusher itself to release its locks. Of course, this\n899: // local view of the dependency graph is incomplete, as it does not initially\n900: // take into consideration transitive dependencies. To address this, when the\n901: // QueryTxn returns to the initial txnWaitQueue, the pusher records its own\n902: // dependencies as dependencies of its pushee transaction. As this process\n903: // continues and pushers periodically query for their own dependencies and\n904: // transfer these to their pushee, each txnWaitQueue accumulate more information\n905: // about the global \"waits-for\" graph. Eventually, one of the txnWaitQueues is\n906: // able to observe a full cycle in this graph and aborts one of the transactions\n907: // in the cycle to break the deadlock.\n908: //\n909: // # Example of Distributed Deadlock Detection\n910: //\n911: // The following diagram demonstrates how the txnWaitQueue interacts with\n912: // distributed deadlock detection.\n913: //\n914: //   - txnA enters txnB's txnWaitQueue during a PushTxn request (MaybeWaitForPush)\n915: //\n916: //   - txnB enters txnC's txnWaitQueue during a PushTxn request (MaybeWaitForPush)\n917: //\n918: //   - txnC enters txnA's txnWaitQueue during a PushTxn request (MaybeWaitForPush)\n919: //\n920: //     .-----------------------------------.\n921: //     |                                   |\n922: //     v                                   |\n923: //     [txnA record] --> [txnB record] --> [txnC record]\n924: //     deps:             deps:             deps:\n925: //\n926: //   - txnC            - txnA            - txnB\n927: //\n928: //   - txnA queries its own txnWaitQueue using a QueryTxn request (MaybeWaitForQuery)\n929: //\n930: //     .-----------------------------------.\n931: //     |    ............                   |\n932: //     v    v          .                   |\n933: //     [txnA record] --> [txnB record] --> [txnC record]\n934: //     deps:             deps:             deps:\n935: //\n936: //   - txnC            - txnA            - txnB\n937: //\n938: //   - txnA finds that txnC is a dependent. It transfers this dependency to txnB\n939: //\n940: //     .-----------------------------------.\n941: //     |                                   |\n942: //     v                                   |\n943: //     [txnA record] --> [txnB record] --> [txnC record]\n944: //     deps:             deps:             deps:\n945: //\n946: //   - txnC            - txnA            - txnB\n947: //\n948: //   - txnC\n949: //\n950: //   - txnC queries its own txnWaitQueue using a QueryTxn request (MaybeWaitForQuery)\n951: //\n952: //   - txnB queries its own txnWaitQueue using a QueryTxn request (MaybeWaitForQuery)\n953: //\n954: //   - txnC finds that txnB is a dependent. It transfers this dependency to txnA\n955: //\n956: //   - txnB finds that txnA and txnC are dependents. It transfers these dependencies to txnC\n957: //\n958: //     .-----------------------------------.\n959: //     |                                   |\n960: //     v                                   |\n961: //     [txnA record] --> [txnB record] --> [txnC record]\n962: //     deps:             deps:             deps:\n963: //\n964: //   - txnC            - txnA            - txnB\n965: //\n966: //   - txnB            - txnC            - txnA\n967: //\n968: //   - txnC\n969: //\n970: //   - txnB notices that txnC is a transitive dependency of itself. This indicates\n971: //     a cycle in the global wait-for graph. txnC is aborted, breaking the cycle\n972: //     and the deadlock\n973: //\n974: //     [txnA record] --> [txnB record] --> [txnC record: ABORTED]\n975: //\n976: //   - txnC releases its locks and the transactions proceed in order.\n977: //\n978: //     [txnA record] --> [txnB record] --> (free to commit)\n979: //\n980: // TODO(nvanbenschoten): if we exposed a \"queue guard\" interface, we could make\n981: // stronger guarantees around cleaning up enqueued txns when there are no\n982: // waiters.\n983: type txnWaitQueue interface {\n984: \trequestQueuer\n985: \n986: \t// EnqueueTxn creates a queue associated with the provided transaction. Once\n987: \t// a queue is established, pushers of this transaction can wait in the queue\n988: \t// and will be informed of state transitions that the transaction undergoes.\n989: \tEnqueueTxn(*roachpb.Transaction)\n990: \n991: \t// UpdateTxn informs the queue that the provided transaction has undergone\n992: \t// a state transition.     "content": "580: //   - a request that is part of a transaction which has already acquired a lock\n581: //     does not need to wait on that lock during sequencing, and can therefore\n582: //     ignore any queue that has formed on the lock.\n583: //\n584: //   - contending requests that encounter different levels of contention may be\n585: //     sequenced in non-FIFO order. This is to allow for more concurrency. e.g.\n586: //     if request R1 and R2 contend on key K2, but R1 is also waiting at key K1,\n587: //     R2 could slip past R1 and evaluate.\n588: type lockTable interface {\n589: \trequestQueuer\n590: \n591: \t// ScanAndEnqueue scans over the spans that the request will access and\n592: \t// enqueues the request in the lock wait-queue of any conflicting locks\n593: \t// encountered.\n594: \t//\n595: \t// The first call to ScanAndEnqueue for a given request uses a nil\n596: \t// lockTableGuard and the subsequent calls reuse the previously returned\n597: \t// one. The latches needed by the request must be held when calling this\n598: \t// function.\n599: \tScanAndEnqueue(Request, lockTableGuard) (lockTableGuard, *Error)\n600: \n601: \t// ScanOptimistic takes a snapshot of the lock table for later checking for\n602: \t// conflicts, and returns a guard. It is for optimistic evaluation of\n603: \t// requests that will typically scan a small subset of the spans mentioned\n604: \t// in the Request. After Request evaluation, CheckOptimisticNoConflicts\n605: \t// must be called on the guard.\n606: \tScanOptimistic(Request) lockTableGuard\n607: \n608: \t// Dequeue removes the request from its lock wait-queues. It should be\n609: \t// called when the request is finished, whether it evaluated or not. The\n610: \t// guard should not be used after being dequeued.\n611: \t//\n612: \t// This method does not release any locks. This method must be called on the\n613: \t// last guard returned from ScanAndEnqueue for the request, even if one of\n614: \t// the (a) lockTable calls that use a lockTableGuard parameter, or (b) a\n615: \t// lockTableGuard call, returned an error. The method allows but does not\n616: \t// require latches to be held.\n617: \tDequeue(lockTableGuard)\n618: \n619: \t// AddDiscoveredLock informs the lockTable of a lock which is wasn't\n620: \t// previously tracking that was discovered during evaluation under the\n621: \t// provided lease sequence.\n622: \t//\n623: \t// The method is called when an exclusive replicated lock held by a\n624: \t// different transaction is discovered when reading the MVCC keys during\n625: \t// evaluation of this request. It adds the lock and enqueues this requester\n626: \t// in its wait-queue. It is required that request evaluation discover such\n627: \t// locks before acquiring its own locks, since the request needs to repeat\n628: \t// ScanAndEnqueue. When consultTxnStatusCache=true, and the transaction\n629: \t// holding the lock is known to be pushed or finalized, the lock is not added\n630: \t// to the lock table and instead tracked in the list of locks to resolve in\n631: \t// the lockTableGuard.\n632: \t//\n633: \t// The lease sequence is used to detect lease changes between the when\n634: \t// request that found the lock started evaluating and when the discovered\n635: \t// lock is added to the lockTable. If there has been a lease change between\n636: \t// these times, information about the discovered lock may be stale, so it is\n637: \t// ignored.\n638: \t//\n639: \t// A latch consistent with the access desired by the guard must be held on\n640: \t// the span containing the discovered lock's key.\n641: \t//\n642: \t// The method returns a boolean indicating whether the discovered lock was\n643: \t// properly handled either by adding it to the lockTable or storing it in\n644: \t// the list of locks to resolve in the lockTableGuard (both cases return\n645: \t// true) or whether it was ignored because the lockTable is currently\n646: \t// disabled (false).\n647: \tAddDiscoveredLock(\n648: \t\tfoundLock *roachpb.Lock, seq roachpb.LeaseSequence,\n649: \t\tconsultTxnStatusCache bool, guard lockTableGuard,\n650: \t) (bool, error)\n651: \n652: \t// AcquireLock informs the lockTable that a new lock was acquired or an\n653: \t// existing lock was updated.\n654: \t//\n655: \t// The TxnMeta associated with the lock acquisition must be the same one used\n656: \t// when the request scanned the lockTable initially. It must only be called in\n657: \t// the evaluation phase, before calling Dequeue, which means all latches\n658: \t// needed by the request are held. The key must be in the request's lock span\n659: \t// set with the appropriate strength. Currently, the only strength with which a\n660: \t// lock can be acquired is Intent[1]. This contract ensures that the lock is\n661: \t// not held in a conflicting manner by a different transaction.\n662: \t// Acquiring a lock that is already held by a transaction upgrades the lock's\n663: \t// timestamp and strength. Any prior sequence numbers at which the lock was\n664: \t// previously held and has since been rolled back are no longer tracked as\n665: \t// well.\n666: \t//\n667: \t// [1] We are in an intermediate state where KV ignores lock strength supplied\n668: \t// by SQL and acquires all locks with Intent locking strength. Notably, this\n669: \t// includes in-memory Exclusive locks acquired for `SELECT FOR UPDATE` queries\n670: \t// as well. While the Intent strength verbiage might be a bit surprising,\n671: \t// there is no meaningful difference when it comes to conflict resolution\n672: \t// between a lock and a request. This is a temporary state, which is bound to\n673: \t// change as we go about supporting additional locking strengths in the lock\n674: \t// table.\n675: \t//\n676: \t// For replicated locks, this must be called after the corresponding write\n677: \t// intent has been applied to the replicated state machine.\n678: \tAcquireLock(*roachpb.LockAcquisition) error\n679: \n680: \t// UpdateLocks informs the lockTable that an existing lock or range of locks\n681: \t// was either updated or released.\n682: \t//\n683: \t// The method is called during intent resolution. For spans containing\n684: \t// Replicated locks, this must be called after intent resolution has been\n685: \t// applied to the replicated state machine. The method itself, however,\n686: \t// ignores the Durability field in the LockUpdate. It can therefore be\n687: \t// used to update locks for a given transaction for all durability levels.\n688: \t//\n689: \t// A latch with SpanReadWrite must be held on span with the lowest timestamp\n690: \t// at which any of the locks could be held. This is explained below.\n691: \t//\n692: \t// Note that spans can be wider than the actual keys on which locks were\n693: \t// acquired, and it is ok if no locks are found or locks held by other\n694: \t// transactions are found (for those lock this call is a noop).\n695: \t//\n696: \t// For COMMITTED or ABORTED transactions, all locks are released.\n697: \t//\n698: \t// For PENDING or STAGING transactions, the behavior is:\n699: \t//\n700: \t// - All replicated locks known to the lockTable are dropped. This is not\n701: ",

concurrency\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"testing\"\n\t\"time\"\n\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvpb\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/isolation\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/lock\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/lockspanset\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/spanset\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/txnwait\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/roachpb\"\n\tclustersettings TestWriteWriteConflictDetection verifies that the lock table correctly detects\n// write-write conflicts between two transactions.\nfunc TestWriteWriteConflictDetection(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\t// Create a lock table with capacity for this test\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\t// Create two transactions with different UUIDs\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// Create requests for the same key with intent locks\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// First request: txn1 writes to key1\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\t// Second request: txn2 writes to the same key1\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\t// Scan and enqueue first request\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, guard1)\n\trequire.False(t, guard1.ShouldWait(), \"first request should not wait\")\n\n\t// Acquire lock for first request\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Scan and enqueue second request - should find conflict\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, guard2)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait(), \"second request should wait for first transaction's lock\")\n\n\t// Check the waiting state\n\tstate, err := guard2.CurState()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, waitFor, state.kind)\n\trequire.Equal(t, txn1.ID, state.txn.ID)\n\trequire.True(t, state.held)\n\n\t// Release the locks\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n}\n\n// TestReadWriteConflictWithSerializableIsolation verifies that serializable\n// transactions detect read-write conflicts.\nfunc TestReadWriteConflictWithSerializableIsolation(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction writes to key\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.False(t, guard1.ShouldWait())\n\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction tries to read the same key\n\t// In serializable isolation, reads should also detect conflicts with writes\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Shared, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, guard2)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait(), \"read should wait for write lock\")\n\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n}\n\n// TestTransactionPriorityConflictResolution verifies that transaction priority\n// influences conflict resolution.\nfunc TestTransactionPriorityConflictResolution(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// Low priority transaction writes first\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.LowUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// High priority transaction tries to write to the same key\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.HighUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction (low priority) acquires lock\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction (high priority) tries to write\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// High priority transaction should wait, but could potentially push low priority\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait())\n\tstate, err := guard2.CurState()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, txn1.ID, state.txn.ID)\n\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n}\n\n// TestLockAcquisitionTimout verifies that lock acquisition can timeout.\nfunc TestLockAcquisitionTimeout(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction acquires lock\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction tries to acquire with a timeout\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:            txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp:      txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans:      lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans:     spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t\tLockWaitPolicy: lock.WaitPolicy_Block,\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait())\n\n\t// In a real scenario with a deadline, the wait would eventually timeout\n\t// For this test, we just verify the wait state is set up correctly\n\tstate, err := guard2.CurState()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, waitFor, state.kind)\n\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n}\n\n// TestIntentResolutionAfterCommit verifies that locks are released after\n// transaction commit.\nfunc TestIntentResolutionAfterCommit(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction acquires lock\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction tries to access the same key\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait(), \"should wait for first transaction's lock\")\n\n\t// Release the lock from first transaction (simulating commit)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\n\t// After dequeue, second transaction's wait state should be updated\n\t// Re-scan to check the new state\n\tguard2_rescan, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, guard2)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tif guard2_rescan != nil && guard2_rescan.ShouldWait() {\n\t\t// Still waiting on something else or lock not fully resolved\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2_rescan)\n\t} else {\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n\t}\n}\n\n// TestIntentResolutionAfterAbort verifies that locks are released after\n// transaction abort.\nfunc TestIntentResolutionAfterAbort(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction acquires lock\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction tries to access\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait())\n\n\t// Simulate first transaction abort - release locks\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\n\t// Rescan to check that second transaction can now proceed\n\tguard2_rescan, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, guard2)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\tif guard2_rescan != nil {\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2_rescan)\n\t} else {\n\t\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n\t}\n}\n\n// TestMultipleWritersQueueing verifies that multiple writers form a queue\n// waiting for a lock.\nfunc TestMultipleWritersQueueing(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// Create three transactions\n\ttxn1 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn3 := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1002},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1002},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction acquires lock\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(txn1, lock.Intent, guard1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Second transaction waits\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn2.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait())\n\n\t// Third transaction also waits\n\treq3 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:       txn3,\n\t\tTimestamp: txn3.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq3.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard3, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req3, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.True(t, guard3.ShouldWait())\n\n\t// Verify queue depth\n\tstate3, err := guard3.CurState()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, waitFor, state3.kind)\n\t// The queue should have other waiters\n\trequire.Greater(t, state3.queuedLockingRequests, 0)\n\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard3)\n}\n\n// TestLockStrengthHierarchy verifies that different lock strengths\n// interact correctly.\nfunc txn1.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard1, err := (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"testing\"\n\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvpb\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/isolation\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/concurrency/lock\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/lockspanset\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/kv/kvserver/spanset\"\n\t\"github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/pkg/roachpb\"\n\tclustersettings TestWriteWriteConflictDetection verifies that the lock table correctly detects\n// write-write conflicts between two transactions.\nfunc TestWriteWriteConflictDetection(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\t// Create a lock table with capacity for this test\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\n\t// Create two transactions with different UUIDs\n\ttxn1Meta := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\ttxn1 := &roachpb.Transaction{\n\t\tTxnMeta:                 *txn1Meta,\n\t\tReadTimestamp:           txn1Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tGlobalUncertaintyLimit:  txn1Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t}\n\n\ttxn2Meta := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\ttxn2 := &roachpb.Transaction{\n\t\tTxnMeta:                 *txn2Meta,\n\t\tReadTimestamp:           txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tGlobalUncertaintyLimit:  txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t}\n\n\t// Create requests for the same key with intent locks\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// First request: txn1 writes to key1\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:        txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp:  txn1Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans:  lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\t// Second request: txn2 writes to the same key1\n\treq2 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:        txn2,\n\t\tTimestamp:  txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans:  lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\t// Scan and enqueue first request\n\tguard1, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req1, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, guard1)\n\trequire.False(t, guard1.ShouldWait(), \"first request should not wait\")\n\n\t// Acquire lock for first request\n\tacq1 := roachpb.MakeLockAcquisition(txn1Meta, key, lock.Replicated, lock.Intent, nil)\n\terr = lt.AcquireLock(&acq1)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Scan and enqueue second request - should find conflict\n\tguard2, err := lt.ScanAndEnqueue(&req2, nil)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, guard2)\n\trequire.True(t, guard2.ShouldWait(), \"second request should wait for first transaction's lock\")\n\n\t// Check the waiting state\n\tstate, err := guard2.CurState()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, waitFor, state.kind)\n\trequire.Equal(t, txn1Meta.ID, state.txn.ID)\n\trequire.True(t, state.held)\n\n\t// Release the locks\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard2)\n}\n\n// TestReadWriteConflictWithSerializableIsolation verifies that serializable\n// transactions detect read-write conflicts.\nfunc TestReadWriteConflictWithSerializableIsolation(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &roachpb.Transaction{\n\t\tTxnMeta:                 *txn2Meta,\n\t\tReadTimestamp:           txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tGlobalUncertaintyLimit:  txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction writes to key\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:        txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp:  txn1Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans: TestTransactionPriorityConflictResolution(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// Low priority txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans:  lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq2.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, key.Next()))\n\n\tguard2, err := 1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn1 := 1001},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1001},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn2 := &roachpb.Transaction{\n\t\tTxnMeta:                 *txn2Meta,\n\t\tReadTimestamp:           txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tGlobalUncertaintyLimit:  txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t}\n\n\t// First transaction acquires lock\n\treq1 := Request{\n\t\tTxn:        txn1,\n\t\tTimestamp:  txn1Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans:  lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans: spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t}\n\treq1.LockSpans.AddLocks(lock.Intent, span(key, txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tLockSpans:      lockspanset.LockSpanSet{},\n\t\tLatchSpans:     spanset.SpanSet{},\n\t\tLockWaitPolicy: 1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\ttxn1 := err)\n\t// Should not wait for its own lock\n\trequire.False(t, guard1_epoch2.ShouldWait())\n\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1)\n\tlt.Dequeue(guard1_epoch2)\n}\n\n// TestIsolationLevelConflicts verifies that TestWriteWriteConflictDetection verifies that the lock table correctly detects\n// write-write conflicts between two transactions.\nfunc TestWriteWriteConflictDetection(t *testing.T) {\n\tdefer leaktest.AfterTest(t)()\n\tdefer log.Scope(t).Close(t)\n\n\tsettings := clustersettings.MakeTestingClusterSettings()\n\tclock := hlc.NewClockForTesting(nil)\n\n\t// Create a lock table with capacity for this test\n\tlt := newLockTable(10000, roachpb.RangeID(1), clock, settings)\n\tlt.enabled = true\n\tlt.enabledSeq = 1\n\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\n\t// Create two transactions with different UUIDs\n\ttxn1Meta := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tPriority:       roachpb.NormalUserPriority,\n\t}\n\n\ttxn1 := &roachpb.Transaction{\n\t\tTxnMeta:                 *txn1Meta,\n\t\tReadTimestamp:           txn1Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tGlobalUncertaintyLimit:  txn1Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t}\n\n\ttxn2Meta := &enginepb.TxnMeta{\n\t\tID:             uuid.Must(uuid.NewV4()),\n\t\tIsoLevel:       isolation.Serializable,\n\t\tEpoch:          1,\n\t\tWriteTimestamp: hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: 1000},\n\t\tMinTimestamp:   hlc.Timestamp{WallTime: txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t\tGlobalUncertaintyLimit:  txn2Meta.WriteTimestamp,\n\t}\n\n\t// Create requests for the same key with intent locks\n\tkey := roachpb.Key(\"key1\")\n\n\t// First request:
